      <p><b>Seychelles</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Seychelles.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4f/En-us-Seychelles.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Seychelles.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <small>French:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[sɛʃɛl]</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <span style="font-size:85%;">or</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[seʃɛl]</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>), officially the <b>Republic of Seychelles</b> (French: <i lang="fr">République des Seychelles</i>; <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole" title="Seychellois Creole">Creole</a>: <i>La Repiblik Sesel</i>), is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelagic</a> <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> at the eastern edge of the Somali Sea. The country consists of 115 islands. Its capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria</a>, lies 1,500 kilometres (932&nbsp;mi) east of mainland <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. Other nearby island countries and territories include the <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/French_Fifth_Republic" title="French Fifth Republic">French</a> <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department_and_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas department and region">overseas regions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> to the south; as well as <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a> (administered by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> as the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a>) to the east. With a population of roughly 98,462,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> it has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_population" title="List of African countries by population">smallest population of any sovereign African country</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Seychelles was uninhabited prior to being encountered by Europeans in the 16th century. It faced competing French and British interests until coming under full British control in the late 18th century. Since proclaiming independence from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> in 1976, Seychelles has developed from a largely agricultural society to a market-based diversified economy, characterized by rapidly rising <a href="/wiki/Service_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Service sector">service</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> activities. From 1976 until 2015, nominal GDP grew nearly sevenfold, and <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> increased nearly sixteenfold. Since the late 2010s, the government has taken steps to encourage foreign investment. </p>
      <p>Today, Seychelles boasts the highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">nominal per capita GDP</a> of any African nation. It is the first African country with an HDI score exceeding 0.800, and is one of the only countries in the continent with a very high <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of African countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>. It is one of only two countries in Africa classified as a <a href="/wiki/High-income_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="High-income economy">high-income economy</a> by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the other being <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>. Despite its relative prosperity, poverty remains widespread as the country has one of the highest levels of <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">economic inequality</a> in the world and markedly unequal <a href="/wiki/Wealth_distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Wealth distribution">wealth distribution</a>, with the upper and ruling class commanding a vast proportion of the country's wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Seychellois culture and society is an eclectic mix of French, British, and African influences, with more recent infusions of Chinese and Indian elements. The country is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Seychelles" title="History of Seychelles">History of Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gama_armada_of_1502_(Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Gama_armada_of_1502_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg/220px-Gama_armada_of_1502_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Gama_armada_of_1502_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg/330px-Gama_armada_of_1502_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Gama_armada_of_1502_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg/440px-Gama_armada_of_1502_%28Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="457"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gama_armada_of_1502_(Livro_de_Lisuarte_de_Abreu).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The first Europeans to discover the Seychelles were the <a href="/wiki/4th_Portuguese_India_Armada_(Gama,_1502)" title="4th Portuguese India Armada (Gama, 1502)">4th Portuguese India Armada</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Seychelles were uninhabited throughout most of recorded history. Some scholars assume that <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Austronesian people">Austronesian</a> seafarers and later <a href="/wiki/Maldive_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Maldive Islands">Maldivian</a> and Arab traders were the first to visit the uninhabited Seychelles. This assumption is based on the discovery of tombs, visible until 1910.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The earliest recorded sighting by Europeans took place on 15 March 1503, recorded by <a href="/wiki/Thom%C3%A9_Lopes" title="Thomé Lopes">Thomé Lopes</a> aboard <i>Rui Mendes de Brito</i>, part of the <a href="/wiki/4th_Portuguese_India_Armada_(Gama,_1502)" title="4th Portuguese India Armada (Gama, 1502)">4th Portuguese India Armada</a> commanded by the Portuguese Admiral <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>. Da Gama's ships passed close to an elevated island, probably <a href="/wiki/Silhouette_Island" title="Silhouette Island">Silhouette Island</a> and the following day <a href="/wiki/Desroches_Island" title="Desroches Island">Desroches Island</a>. The earliest recorded landing was in January 1609, by the crew of the <i>Ascension</i> under Captain <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Sharpeigh" title="Alexander Sharpeigh">Alexander Sharpeigh</a> during the fourth voyage of the British <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>. </p>
      <p>A transit point for trade between Africa and Asia, the islands were said to be occasionally used by <a href="/wiki/Pirates" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirates">pirates</a> until the French began to take control starting in 1756 when a Stone of Possession was laid on <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_Seychelles" title="Mahé, Seychelles">Mahé</a> by Captain <a href="/wiki/Corneille_Nicholas_Morphey" title="Corneille Nicholas Morphey">Nicholas Morphey</a>. The islands were named after <a href="/wiki/Jean_Moreau_de_S%C3%A9chelles" title="Jean Moreau de Séchelles">Jean Moreau de Séchelles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_XV" title="Louis XV">Louis XV</a>'s Minister of Finance.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The British frigate <i>Orpheus</i> commanded by Captain Henry Newcome arrived at Mahé on 16 May 1794, during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_First_Coalition" title="War of the First Coalition">War of the First Coalition</a>. Terms of capitulation were drawn up and the next day Seychelles was surrendered to Britain. Jean Baptiste Quéau de Quincy, the French administrator of Seychelles during the years of war with the United Kingdom, declined to resist when armed enemy warships arrived. Instead, he successfully negotiated the status of capitulation to Britain which gave the settlers a privileged position of neutrality. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_1953_coronation_stamp.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Seychelles_1953_coronation_stamp.JPG/140px-Seychelles_1953_coronation_stamp.JPG" decoding="async" width="140" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Seychelles_1953_coronation_stamp.JPG/210px-Seychelles_1953_coronation_stamp.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Seychelles_1953_coronation_stamp.JPG/280px-Seychelles_1953_coronation_stamp.JPG 2x" data-file-width="383" data-file-height="500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_1953_coronation_stamp.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>1953 stamp with portrait of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Britain eventually assumed full control upon the surrender of <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> in 1810, formalised in 1814 at the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1814)" title="Treaty of Paris (1814)">Treaty of Paris</a>. Seychelles became a <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a> separate from Mauritius in 1903. Elections were held in 1966 and 1970. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Seychelles_1900s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Victoria_Seychelles_1900s.jpg/220px-Victoria_Seychelles_1900s.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Victoria_Seychelles_1900s.jpg/330px-Victoria_Seychelles_1900s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Victoria_Seychelles_1900s.jpg/440px-Victoria_Seychelles_1900s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="463"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Seychelles_1900s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Victoria, Seychelles 1900s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Independence was granted in 1976 and it became a republic at the same time. It has been a member of <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Seychelles_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Seychelles-14">[14]</a></sup> In the 1970s Seychelles was "the place to be seen, a playground for film stars and the international jet set".<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-15">[15]</a></sup> In 1977, a <a href="/wiki/1977_Seychelles_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1977 Seychelles coup d'état">coup d'état</a> by <a href="/wiki/France_Albert_Ren%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="France Albert René">France Albert René</a> ousted the first president of the republic, <a href="/wiki/James_Mancham" title="James Mancham">James Mancham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-africanhistory.about.com_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africanhistory.about.com-16">[16]</a></sup> René discouraged overdependence on tourism and declared that he wanted "to keep the Seychelles for the Seychellois".<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 1979 constitution declared a socialist one-party state, which lasted until 1991. </p>
      <p>In the 1980s there were a series of coup attempts against President René, some of which were supported by South Africa. In 1981, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Hoare" class="mw-redirect" title="Mike Hoare">Mike Hoare</a> led a team of 43 South African mercenaries masquerading as holidaying rugby players in the <a href="/wiki/1981_Seychelles_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1981 Seychelles coup d'état attempt">1981 Seychelles coup d'état attempt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-15">[15]</a></sup> There was a gun battle at the airport, and most of the mercenaries later escaped in a hijacked <a href="/wiki/Air_India" title="Air India">Air India</a> plane.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-15">[15]</a></sup> The leader of this hijacking was German mercenary D. Clodo, a former member of the Rhodesian SAS.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Clodo later stood trial in South Africa (where he was acquitted) as well as in his home country Germany for air piracy.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1986, an attempted coup led by the Seychelles Minister of Defence, Ogilvy Berlouis, caused President René to request assistance from India. In <a href="/wiki/Operation_Flowers_are_Blooming" title="Operation Flowers are Blooming">Operation Flowers are Blooming</a>, the Indian naval vessel <a href="/wiki/INS_Vindhyagiri" title="INS Vindhyagiri"><i>Vindhyagiri</i></a> arrived in Port Victoria to help avert the coup.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first draft of a new constitution failed to receive the requisite 60% of voters in 1992, but an amended version was approved in 1993. </p>
      <p>In January 2013, Seychelles declared a state of emergency; the tropical cyclone Felleng caused torrential rain, and flooding and landslides destroyed hundreds of houses.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AL_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AL-21">[21]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Victoria.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Victoria.jpeg/220px-Victoria.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Victoria.jpeg/330px-Victoria.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Victoria.jpeg/440px-Victoria.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="935" data-file-height="702"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Victoria.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria</a>, the capital of Seychelles
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Seychelles" title="Politics of Seychelles">Politics of Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Seychelles president, who is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, is elected by popular vote for a five(5) year term of office. The cabinet is presided over and appointed by the president, subject to the approval of a majority of the legislature. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> Seychellois parliament, <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Seychelles)" title="National Assembly (Seychelles)">the National Assembly</a> or <i>Assemblée Nationale</i>, consists of 35 members, 26 of whom are elected directly by popular vote, while the remaining nine seats are appointed proportionally according to the percentage of votes received by each party. All members serve five-year terms. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Seychelles" title="Supreme Court of Seychelles">Supreme Court of Seychelles</a>, created in 1903, is the highest trial court in Seychelles and the first court of appeal from all the lower courts and tribunals. The highest court of law in Seychelles is the Seychelles Court of Appeal, which is the court of final appeal in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:James_Michel_in_meeting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/James_Michel_in_meeting.jpg/220px-James_Michel_in_meeting.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/James_Michel_in_meeting.jpg/330px-James_Michel_in_meeting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/James_Michel_in_meeting.jpg/440px-James_Michel_in_meeting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1648" data-file-height="1276"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:James_Michel_in_meeting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Then-President <a href="/wiki/James_Michel" title="James Michel">James Michel</a> in his office in <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria</a>, 2009
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Seychelles' first president <a href="/wiki/France_Albert_Ren%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="France Albert René">France Albert René</a> came to power after his supporters overthrew the first president <a href="/wiki/James_Mancham" title="James Mancham">James Mancham</a> on 5 June 1977 in a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> and installed him as president. René was at that time the prime minister. René ruled as a <a href="/wiki/Strongman_(politics)" title="Strongman (politics)">strongman</a> under a <a href="/wiki/Socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist">socialist</a> <a href="/wiki/One-party_system" class="mw-redirect" title="One-party system">one-party system</a> until 1993, when he was forced to introduce a multi-party system. He stepped down in 2004 in favour of his vice-president, <a href="/wiki/James_Michel" title="James Michel">James Michel</a>, who was reelected in 2006 and again in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Seychelles_Nation_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seychelles_Nation-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Agence_France-Presse_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agence_France-Presse-25">[25]</a></sup> On 28 September 2016, the Office of the President announced that Michel would step down effective 16 October, and that Vice President <a href="/wiki/Danny_Faure" title="Danny Faure">Danny Faure</a> would complete the rest of Michel's term.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 26th October 2020, <a href="/wiki/Wavel_Ramkalawan" title="Wavel Ramkalawan">Wavel Ramkalawan</a>, a 59 year old Anglican priest was elected the fifth President of the Republic of Seychelles. Ramkalawan was an opposition MP from 1993 to 2011, and from 2016 to 2020. He served as the Leader of the Opposition from 1998 to 2011 and from 2016 to 2020. Ramkalawan defeated incumbent Danny Faure by 54.9% to 43.5%. This marked the first time the opposition had won a presidential election.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The primary political parties are the former ruling socialist <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Seychelles)" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Party (Seychelles)">People's Party</a> (PP), known until 2009 as the Seychelles People's Progressive Front (SPPF) now called <a href="/wiki/United_Seychelles" title="United Seychelles">United Seychelles</a> (US), and the <a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">socially liberal</a> <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_National_Party" title="Seychelles National Party">Seychelles National Party</a> (SNP).<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The election of the National Assembly was held on the 22-24 October 2020. The Seychelles National Party, the Seychelles Party for Social Justice and Democracy and the Seychelles United Party formed a coalition, <a href="/wiki/Linyon_Demokratik_Seselwa" title="Linyon Demokratik Seselwa">Linyon Demokratik Seselwa</a> (LDS). LDS won 25 seats and US 10 seats of the 35 seats of the National Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Seychelles" title="Foreign relations of Seychelles">Foreign relations of Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Seychelles is a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (<b>AU</b>), the francophone <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Commission" title="Indian Ocean Commission">Indian Ocean Commission</a> (IOC), <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (<b>SADC</b>) and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>. From 1979 to 1981, the United States and South Africa were involved in the failed 1981 <a href="/wiki/1981_Seychelles_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1981 Seychelles coup d'état attempt">coup attempt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Under the Obama administration, the US began running drone operations out of Seychelles.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-32">[32]</a></sup> In the Spring of 2013, members of the Special-Purpose Marine Air-Ground Task Force Africa mentored troops in Seychelles, along with a variety of other African nations.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Seychelles" title="Districts of Seychelles">Districts of Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Seychelles is divided into twenty-six administrative regions comprising all of the inner islands. Eight of the districts make up the capital of Seychelles and are referred to as Greater <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria</a>. Another 14 districts are considered the rural part of the main island of <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_Seychelles" title="Mahé, Seychelles">Mahé</a> with two districts on <a href="/wiki/Praslin" title="Praslin">Praslin</a> and one on <a href="/wiki/La_Digue" title="La Digue">La Digue</a> which also includes respective satellite islands. The rest of the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Islands_(Seychelles)" title="Outer Islands (Seychelles)">Outer Islands</a> (<i><i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Îles Eloignées</i></i>) are the last district recently created by the tourism ministry. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Seychelles" title="Geography of Seychelles">Geography of Seychelles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Seychelles" title="Geology of Seychelles">Geology of Seychelles</a>

      </div> 
      <p>An island nation, Seychelles is located in the Somali Sea segment of the Indian Ocean, northeast of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> and about 1,600&nbsp;km (994&nbsp;mi) east of <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>. The Constitution of Seychelles lists 155 (not 115) named islands <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://greybook.seylii.org/w/se/CAP42#!fragment//BQCwhgziBcwMYgK4DsDWszIQewE4BUBTADwBdoByCgSgBpltTCIBFRQ3AT0otokLC4EbDtyp8BQkAGU8pAELcASgFEAMioBqAQQByAYRW1SYAEbRS2ONWpA">Constitution of Seychelles</a> and a further 7 reclaimed islands have been created subsequent to the publication of the Constitution. The majority of the islands are uninhabited, with many dedicated as nature reserves. Seychelles largest island Mahe is located at a distance of 835&nbsp;mi (1,344&nbsp;km), from Mogadishu, Somalia's capital over the Somali Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A group of 44 islands (42 granitic and 2 coralline) occupy the shallow waters of the Seychelles Bank and are collectively referred to as the inner islands. They have a total area of 244&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>, accounting for 54% of the total land area of the Seychelles and 98% of the entire population. </p>
      <p>The islands are divided into groups as follows. </p>
      <p>There are 42 granitic islands known as the <a href="/wiki/Granitic_Seychelles" title="Granitic Seychelles">Granitic Seychelles</a>. These are in descending order of size: <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_Seychelles" title="Mahé, Seychelles">Mahé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Praslin" title="Praslin">Praslin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silhouette_Island" title="Silhouette Island">Silhouette Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Digue" title="La Digue">La Digue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curieuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Curieuse">Curieuse</a>, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9licit%C3%A9_Island" title="Félicité Island">Félicité</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9gate_Island" title="Frégate Island">Frégate</a>, Ste-Anne, North, Cerf, Marianne, Grand Sœur, Thérèse, <a href="/wiki/Aride_Island" title="Aride Island">Aride Island</a>, Conception, Petite Sœur, <a href="/wiki/Cousin_Island" title="Cousin Island">Cousin Island</a>, Cousine, Long, Récif, Round (Praslin), Anonyme, Mamelles, <a href="/wiki/Moyenne_Island" title="Moyenne Island">Moyenne</a>, Île aux Vaches Marines, L'Islette, Beacon (Île Sèche), <a href="/wiki/Cach%C3%A9e_Island" title="Cachée Island">Cachée</a>, Cocos, Round (Mahé), L'Ilot Frégate, Booby, Chauve-Souris (Mahé), Chauve-Souris (Praslin), Île La Fouche, Hodoul, L'Ilot, Rat, Souris, St. Pierre (Praslin), Zavé, Harrison Rocks (Grand Rocher). </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Anse_Source_d%27Argent_2-La_Digue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Anse_Source_d%27Argent_2-La_Digue.jpg/220px-Anse_Source_d%27Argent_2-La_Digue.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Anse_Source_d%27Argent_2-La_Digue.jpg/330px-Anse_Source_d%27Argent_2-La_Digue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Anse_Source_d%27Argent_2-La_Digue.jpg/440px-Anse_Source_d%27Argent_2-La_Digue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1435"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Anse_Source_d%27Argent_2-La_Digue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Beach of Anse Source d'Argent on the island of <a href="/wiki/La_Digue" title="La Digue">La Digue</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are two coral sand <a href="/wiki/Cay" title="Cay">cays</a> north of the granitics on the edge of the Seychelles Bank: <a href="/wiki/Denis_Island" title="Denis Island">Denis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bird_Island,_Seychelles" title="Bird Island, Seychelles">Bird</a>. </p>
      <p>There are two <a href="/wiki/Coral_island" title="Coral island">coral islands</a> south of the Granitics: <a href="/wiki/Co%C3%ABtivy_Island" title="Coëtivy Island">Coëtivy</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_Platte" title="Île Platte">Platte</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Anse_Lazio_beach_Praslin_Seychelles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Anse_Lazio_beach_Praslin_Seychelles.jpg/220px-Anse_Lazio_beach_Praslin_Seychelles.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Anse_Lazio_beach_Praslin_Seychelles.jpg/330px-Anse_Lazio_beach_Praslin_Seychelles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Anse_Lazio_beach_Praslin_Seychelles.jpg/440px-Anse_Lazio_beach_Praslin_Seychelles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Anse_Lazio_beach_Praslin_Seychelles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Beach of <a href="/wiki/Anse_Lazio" title="Anse Lazio">Anse Lazio</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Praslin" title="Praslin">Praslin</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are 29 coral islands in the <a href="/wiki/Amirantes" class="mw-redirect" title="Amirantes">Amirantes group</a>, west of the granitics: <a href="/wiki/Desroches" class="mw-redirect" title="Desroches">Desroches</a>, Poivre Atoll (comprising three islands—Poivre, Florentin and South Island), Alphonse, D'Arros, St. Joseph Atoll (comprising 14 islands—St. Joseph, Île aux Fouquets, Resource, Petit Carcassaye, Grand Carcassaye, Benjamin, Bancs Ferrari, Chiens, Pélicans, Vars, Île Paul, Banc de Sable, Banc aux Cocos and Île aux Poules), Marie Louise, Desnœufs, African Banks (comprising two islands—African Banks and South Island), Rémire, St. François, Boudeuse, Étoile, Bijoutier. </p>
      <p>There are 13 coral islands in the <a href="/wiki/Farquhar_Group" title="Farquhar Group">Farquhar Group</a>, south-southwest of the Amirantes: <a href="/wiki/Farquhar_Atoll" title="Farquhar Atoll">Farquhar Atoll</a> (comprising 10 islands—Bancs de Sable, Déposés, Île aux Goëlettes, Lapins, Île du Milieu, North Manaha, South Manaha, Middle Manaha, North Island and South Island), Providence Atoll (comprising two islands—Providence and Bancs Providence) and St Pierre. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_017.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Seychelles_017.JPG/220px-Seychelles_017.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Seychelles_017.JPG/330px-Seychelles_017.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Seychelles_017.JPG/440px-Seychelles_017.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_017.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mahé Island
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are 67 <a href="/wiki/Raised_coral_atoll" title="Raised coral atoll">raised coral islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Aldabra_Group" title="Aldabra Group">Aldabra Group</a>, west of the Farquhar Group: <a href="/wiki/Aldabra_Atoll" class="mw-redirect" title="Aldabra Atoll">Aldabra Atoll</a> (comprising 46 islands—Grande Terre, Picard, Polymnie, Malabar, Île Michel, Île Esprit, Île aux Moustiques, Ilot Parc, Ilot Émile, Ilot Yangue, Ilot Magnan, Île Lanier, Champignon des Os, Euphrate, Grand Mentor, Grand Ilot, Gros Ilot Gionnet, Gros Ilot Sésame, Héron Rock, Hide Island, Île aux Aigrettes, Île aux Cèdres, Îles Chalands, Île Fangame, Île Héron, Île Michel, Île Squacco, Île Sylvestre, Île Verte, Ilot Déder, Ilot du Sud, Ilot du Milieu, Ilot du Nord, Ilot Dubois, Ilot Macoa, Ilot Marquoix, Ilots Niçois, Ilot Salade, Middle Row Island, Noddy Rock, North Row Island, Petit Mentor, Petit Mentor Endans, Petits Ilots, Pink Rock and Table Ronde), <a href="/wiki/Assumption_Island" title="Assumption Island">Assumption Island</a>, Astove and <a href="/wiki/Cosmoledo_Atoll" class="mw-redirect" title="Cosmoledo Atoll">Cosmoledo Atoll</a> (comprising 19 islands—Menai, Île du Nord (West North), Île Nord-Est (East North), Île du Trou, Goélettes, Grand Polyte, Petit Polyte, Grand Île (Wizard), Pagode, Île du Sud-Ouest (South), Île aux Moustiques, Île Baleine, Île aux Chauve-Souris, Île aux Macaques, Île aux Rats, Île du Nord-Ouest, Île Observation, Île Sud-Est and Ilot la Croix). </p>
      <p>In addition to these 155 islands as per the Constitution of Seychelles there are 7 reclaimed islands: Ile Perseverance, Ile Aurore, Romainville, Eden Island, Eve, Ile du Port and Ile Soleil. </p>
      <p>South Island, African Banks has been eroded by the sea. At St Joseph Atoll, Banc de Sable and Pelican Island have also eroded, while Grand Carcassaye and Petit Carcassaye have merged to form one island. There are also several unnamed islands at Aldabra, St Joseph Atoll and Cosmoledo. Pti Astove, though named, failed to make it into the Constitution for unknown reasons. Bancs Providence is not a single island, but a dynamic group of islands, comprising four large and about six very small islets in 2016. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The climate is equable although quite humid, as the islands are small,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> classified by <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen-Geiger_climate_classification_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Köppen-Geiger climate classification system">Köppen-Geiger system</a> as <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rain_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical rain forest">tropical rain forest</a> (Af). The temperature varies little throughout the year. Temperatures on Mahé vary from 24 to 30&nbsp;°C (75 to 86&nbsp;°F), and rainfall ranges from 2,900&nbsp;mm (114&nbsp;in) annually at <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria</a> to 3,600&nbsp;mm (142&nbsp;in) on the mountain slopes. <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> is somewhat less on the other islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the coolest months, July and August, the average low is about 24&nbsp;°C (75&nbsp;°F). The southeast trade winds blow regularly from May to November, and this is the most pleasant time of the year. The hot months are from December to April, with higher humidity (80%). March and April are the hottest months, but the temperature seldom exceeds 31&nbsp;°C (88&nbsp;°F). Most of the islands lie outside the cyclone belt, so high winds are rare.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flora_and_fauna_of_Seychelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Flora and fauna of Seychelles">Flora and fauna of Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:115px;max-width:115px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:219px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg/113px-Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg" decoding="async" width="113" height="219" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg/170px-Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg/226px-Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg 2x" data-file-width="515" data-file-height="1000"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:173px;max-width:173px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:219px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg/171px-Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg" decoding="async" width="171" height="219" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg/257px-Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg/342px-Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2179" data-file-height="2792"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          Left: Seychelles paradise-flycatcher; right: bird flocks on Bird Island Seychelles
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG/170px-Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG/255px-Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG/340px-Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3467" data-file-height="3751"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An Aldabra giant tortoise
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Seychelles is among the world's leading countries to protect lands for <a href="/wiki/Threatened_species" title="Threatened species">threatened species</a>, allocating 42% of its territory for <a href="/wiki/Conservation_(ethic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservation (ethic)">conservation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Like many fragile island ecosystems, Seychelles saw the loss of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> when humans first settled in the area, including the disappearance of most of the <a href="/wiki/Aldabrachelys" title="Aldabrachelys">giant tortoises</a> from the granitic islands, the felling of coastal and mid-level forests, and the extinction of species such as the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_chestnut-flanked_white-eye" class="mw-redirect" title="Seychelles chestnut-flanked white-eye">chestnut flanked white eye</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_parakeet" title="Seychelles parakeet">Seychelles parakeet</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Saltwater_crocodile" title="Saltwater crocodile">saltwater crocodile</a>. However, extinctions were far fewer than on islands such as <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, partly due to a shorter period of human occupation (since 1770). Seychelles today is known for success stories in protecting its flora and fauna. The rare <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_black_parrot" title="Seychelles black parrot">Seychelles black parrot</a>, the national bird of the country, is now protected. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Freshwater_crab" title="Freshwater crab">freshwater crab</a> genus <i><a href="/wiki/Seychellum" title="Seychellum">Seychellum</a></i> is endemic to the granitic Seychelles, and a further 26 species of crabs and five species of <a href="/wiki/Hermit_crab" title="Hermit crab">hermit crabs</a> live on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Haig_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haig-39">[39]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Aldabra_giant_tortoise" title="Aldabra giant tortoise">Aldabra giant tortoise</a> now populates many of the islands of Seychelles; the Aldabra population is the largest remaining. These unique reptiles can be found even in captive herds. The granitic islands of Seychelles may support distinct species of <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_giant_tortoise" class="mw-redirect" title="Seychelles giant tortoise">Seychelles giant tortoises</a>; the status of the different populations is currently unclear. Seychelles hosts some of the largest <a href="/wiki/Bird_colony" title="Bird colony">seabird colonies</a> in the world, notably on the outer islands of Aldabra and Cosmoledo. In <a href="/wiki/Granitic_Seychelles" title="Granitic Seychelles">granitic Seychelles</a> the largest colonies are on <a href="/wiki/Aride_Island" title="Aride Island">Aride Island</a> including the world's largest numbers of two species. Sooty terns also breed on the islands. Other birds include Cattle egrets (<i>Bubulcus ibis</i>) and Fairy terns (<i>Gygis alba</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> More than 1,000 species of fish have been recorded. </p>
      <p>The granitic islands of Seychelles are home to about 75 endemic plant species, with a further 25 or so species in the <a href="/wiki/Aldabra" title="Aldabra">Aldabra</a> group. Particularly well known is the <a href="/wiki/Coco_de_mer" class="mw-redirect" title="Coco de mer">coco de mer</a>, a species of palm that grows only on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Praslin" title="Praslin">Praslin</a> and neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Curieuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Curieuse">Curieuse</a>. Sometimes nicknamed the "love nut" because the shape of its "double" coconut resembles buttocks, the coco-de-mer produces the world's heaviest seed. The <a href="/wiki/Jellyfish_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Jellyfish tree">jellyfish tree</a> is to be found in only a few locations on <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_Seychelles" title="Mahé, Seychelles">Mahe</a>. This strange and ancient plant in a genus of its own (<i><a href="/wiki/Medusagyne" title="Medusagyne">Medusagyne</a></i>) seems to reproduce only in cultivation and not in the wild. Other unique plant species include Wright's gardenia (<i><a href="/wiki/Rothmannia_annae" title="Rothmannia annae">Rothmannia annae</a></i>) found only on <a href="/wiki/Aride_Island" title="Aride Island">Aride Island</a> Special Reserve. There are several unique species of orchid on the islands. </p>
      <p>Seychelles is home to two terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Granitic_Seychelles_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Granitic Seychelles forests">Granitic Seychelles forests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aldabra_Island_xeric_scrub" class="mw-redirect" title="Aldabra Island xeric scrub">Aldabra Island xeric scrub</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-41">[41]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 10/10, ranking it first globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Since the use of <a href="/wiki/Speargun" title="Speargun">spearguns</a> and dynamite for fishing was banned through efforts of local conservationists in the 1960s, the wildlife is unafraid of <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">snorkelers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">divers</a>. <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching" title="Coral bleaching">Coral bleaching</a> in 1998 has damaged most reefs, but some reefs show healthy recovery (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Silhouette_Island" title="Silhouette Island">Silhouette Island</a>). </p>
      <p>Despite huge disparities across nations,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Seychelles claims to have achieved nearly all of its <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> 17 MDGS and 169 targets have been achieved.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Environmental protection is becoming a cultural value.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Their government's Seychelles Climate Guide describes the nation's climate as rainy, with a dry season with an ocean economy in the ocean regions. The Southeast Trades is on the decline but still fairly strong.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Reportedly, weather patterns there are becoming less predictable.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Seychelles" title="Demographics of Seychelles">Demographics of Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Indo-Seychellois" title="Indo-Seychellois">Indo-Seychellois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sino-Seychellois" title="Sino-Seychellois">Sino-Seychellois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Seychellois Creole People">Seychellois Creole People</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole" title="Seychellois Creole">Seychellois Creole</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Franco-Seychellois" title="Franco-Seychellois">Franco-Seychellois</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ile_de_Mahe_-_Victoria_(9).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ile_de_Mahe_-_Victoria_%289%29.JPG/280px-Ile_de_Mahe_-_Victoria_%289%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="280" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ile_de_Mahe_-_Victoria_%289%29.JPG/420px-Ile_de_Mahe_-_Victoria_%289%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ile_de_Mahe_-_Victoria_%289%29.JPG/560px-Ile_de_Mahe_-_Victoria_%289%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ile_de_Mahe_-_Victoria_(9).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Skyline of <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria</a>, capital and largest city Seychelles
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>When the British gained control of the islands during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, they allowed the French upper class to retain their land. Both the French and British settlers used enslaved Africans, and although the British prohibited slavery in 1835, African workers continued to come. Thus the <i>Gran blan</i> ("big whites") of French origin dominated economic and political life. The British administration employed Indians on <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" class="mw-redirect" title="Indentured servant">indentured servitude</a> to the same degree as in Mauritius resulting in a small Indian population. The Indians, like a similar minority of Chinese, were confined to a merchant class.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Through harmonious socioeconomic policies and developments<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> over the years, today Seychelles is described as a fusion of peoples and cultures. Numerous Seychellois are considered multiracial: blending from African, Asian and European descent to create a modern creole culture. Evidence of this harmonious blend is also revealed in Seychellois food, incorporating various aspects of French, Chinese, Indian and African cuisine. </p>
      <p>As the islands of the Seychelles had no indigenous population, the current Seychellois descend from people who immigrated, of which the largest ethnic groups were those of African, French, <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">Indian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> origin. The median age of the Seychellois is 32 years.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-47">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> are official languages along with <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole" title="Seychellois Creole">Seychellois Creole</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole" class="mw-redirect" title="French-based creole">French-based</a> <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole language</a>. Seychellois Creole is the most widely spoken native language and de facto the <a href="/wiki/National_language" title="National language">national language</a> of the country. Nowadays, Seychellois Creole is often laced with English words and phrases.<sup id="cite_ref-ethno_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethno-48">[48]</a></sup> About 91% of the population are native speakers of Seychelles Creole, 5.1% of English and 0.7% of French.<sup id="cite_ref-ethno_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethno-48">[48]</a></sup> Most business and official meetings are conducted in English and nearly all official websites are in English. National Assembly business is conducted in Creole, but laws are passed and published in English. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Seychelles" title="Religion in Seychelles">Religion in Seychelles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Seychelles" title="Hinduism in Seychelles">Hinduism in Seychelles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Seychelles" title="Islam in Seychelles">Islam in Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:293px;max-width:293px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:157px;max-width:157px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg/155px-St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg" decoding="async" width="155" height="174" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg/233px-St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg/310px-St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1859" data-file-height="2084"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           St Francis Church, Mahé
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:132px;max-width:132px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Hindu_Temple_Victoria_Seychelles_Islands_of_Africa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Hindu_Temple_Victoria_Seychelles_Islands_of_Africa.jpg/130px-Hindu_Temple_Victoria_Seychelles_Islands_of_Africa.jpg" decoding="async" width="130" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Hindu_Temple_Victoria_Seychelles_Islands_of_Africa.jpg/195px-Hindu_Temple_Victoria_Seychelles_Islands_of_Africa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Hindu_Temple_Victoria_Seychelles_Islands_of_Africa.jpg/260px-Hindu_Temple_Victoria_Seychelles_Islands_of_Africa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Seychelles" title="Hinduism in Seychelles">Hindu Temple in Victoria</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the 2010 census, most Seychellois are Christians: 76.2% were <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Seychelles" title="Catholic Church in Seychelles">Roman Catholic</a>, pastorally served by the exempt <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Port_Victoria" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Port Victoria">Diocese of Port Victoria</a> (immediately dependent on the Holy See); 10.6% were Protestant, (<a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a> 6.1%, <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostal Assembly</a> 1.5%, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-Day Adventist</a> 1.2%, other Protestant 1.6%).<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> is the second largest <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a>, with more than 2.4% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-47">[47]</a></sup> A reported 6% of the population of Seychelles are ethnic Indians, but only 2.4% are Hindus.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Islam is followed by another 1.6% of the population. Other faiths accounted for 1.1% of the population, while a further 5.9% were non-religious or did not specify a religion.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-47">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Seychelles" title="Economy of Seychelles">Economy of Seychelles</a>
      </div>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg/220px-Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg/330px-Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg/440px-Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Colourful skirts at Seychelles market
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the plantation era, <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a> were the chief exports. In 1965, during a three-month visit to the islands, futurist <a href="/wiki/Donald_Prell" title="Donald Prell">Donald Prell</a> prepared for the then-<a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a> Governor General an economic report containing a scenario for the future of the economy. Quoting from his report, in the 1960s, about 33% of the working population worked at plantations, and 20% worked in the public or government sector.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The Indian Ocean Tracking Station on Mahé used by the <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_Satellite_Control_Network" title="Air Force Satellite Control Network">Air Force Satellite Control Network</a> was closed in August 1996 after the Seychelles government attempted to raise the rent to more than $10,000,000 per year. </p>
      <p>Since independence in 1976, per capita output has expanded to roughly seven times the old near-subsistence level. Growth has been led by the tourist sector, which employs about 30% of the labour force, compared to agriculture which today employs about 3% of the labour force. Despite the growth of tourism, farming and fishing continue to employ some people, as do industries that process coconuts and vanilla. </p>
      <p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the main export products are processed fish (60%) and non-fillet frozen fish (22%).<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The prime agricultural products currently produced in Seychelles include <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweet potatoes">sweet potatoes</a>, vanilla, coconuts and cinnamon. These products provide much of the economic support of the locals. Frozen and canned fish, copra, cinnamon and vanilla are the main export commodities. </p>
      <p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">worldwide economic crises of 2008</a>, the Seychelles government has prioritised a curbing of the <a href="/wiki/Budget_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Budget deficit">budget deficit</a>, including the containment of <a href="/wiki/Social_welfare" class="mw-redirect" title="Social welfare">social welfare</a> costs and further <a href="/wiki/Privatisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Privatisation">privatisation</a> of public enterprises. The government has a pervasive presence in economic activity, with public enterprises active in petroleum product distribution, banking, imports of basic products, telecommunications and a wide range of other businesses. According to the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a>, which measures the degree of limited government, market openness, regulatory efficiency, rule of law, and other factors, economic freedom has been increasing each year since 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The national currency of Seychelles is the <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_rupee" title="Seychellois rupee">Seychellois rupee</a>. Initially tied to a basket of international currencies, it was depegged and allowed to be devalued and float freely in 2008 on the presumed hopes of attracting further foreign investment in the Seychelles economy. </p>
      <p>Seychelles has emerged the least corrupt country in Africa in the latest Corruption Perception Index (CPI) report released by Transparency International in January 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Seychelles" title="Tourism in Seychelles">Tourism in Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:General_hotel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/General_hotel.jpg/220px-General_hotel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/General_hotel.jpg/330px-General_hotel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/General_hotel.jpg/440px-General_hotel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:General_hotel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Beach resort at Seychelles
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_083.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Seychelles_083.JPG/220px-Seychelles_083.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Seychelles_083.JPG/330px-Seychelles_083.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Seychelles_083.JPG/440px-Seychelles_083.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_083.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Aircraft at <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_International_Airport" title="Seychelles International Airport">Seychelles International Airport</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1971, with the opening of <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_International_Airport" title="Seychelles International Airport">Seychelles International Airport</a>, tourism became a significant industry, essentially dividing the economy into plantations and tourism. The tourism sector paid better, and the plantation economy could only expand so far. The plantation sector of the economy declined in prominence, and tourism became the primary industry of Seychelles. Consequently, there was a sustained spate of hotel construction throughout almost the entire 1970s which included the opening of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coral_Strand_Smart_Choice&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coral Strand Smart Choice (page does not exist)">Coral Strand Smart Choice</a>, Vista Do Mar and Bougainville Hotel in 1972. </p>
      <p>In recent years the government has encouraged foreign investment to upgrade hotels and other services. These incentives have given rise to an enormous amount of investment in real estate projects and new resort properties, such as project TIME, distributed by the World Bank, along with its predecessor project MAGIC.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Despite its growth, the vulnerability of the tourist sector was illustrated by the sharp drop in 1991–1992 due largely to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since then the government has moved to reduce the dependence on tourism by promoting the development of farming, fishing, small-scale manufacturing and most recently the offshore financial sector, through the establishment of the Financial Services Authority and the enactment of several pieces of legislation (such as the International Corporate Service Providers Act, the International Business Companies Act, the Securities Act, the Mutual Funds and Hedge Fund Act, amongst others). In March 2015, Seychelles allocated <a href="/wiki/Assumption_Island" title="Assumption Island">Assumption Island</a> to be developed by India.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Although multinational oil companies have explored the waters around the islands, no oil or gas has been found. In 2005, a deal was signed with US firm Petroquest, giving it exploration rights to about 30,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> around Constant, Topaz, Farquhar and Coëtivy islands until 2014. Seychelles imports oil from the Persian Gulf in the form of refined petroleum derivatives at the rate of about 5,700 barrels per day (910&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>/d). </p>
      <p>In recent years oil has been imported from Kuwait and also from Bahrain. Seychelles imports three times more oil than is needed for internal uses because it re-exports the surplus oil in the form of <a href="/wiki/Bunker_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bunker fuel">bunker</a> for ships and aircraft calling at <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_Seychelles" title="Mahé, Seychelles">Mahé</a>. There are no refining capacities on the islands. Oil and gas imports, distribution and re-export are the responsibility of Seychelles Petroleum (Sepec), while oil exploration is the responsibility of the Seychelles National Oil Company (SNOC). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.
