          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The Seychelles has a diverse and upcoming group of artists who draw inspiration from the Islands around them. </p>
      <p>A National Art Gallery was inaugurated in 1994 on the occasion of the official opening of the National Cultural Centre which housed the National Library and the National Archives with other offices of the Ministry of Culture. </p>
      <p>The Minister of Culture then said that an exhibition which featured the works of artists, painters and sculptors was a testimony to the development of art in Seychelles as a creative form of expression and gave a view of the state of contemporary art in Seychelles. </p>
      <p>Contemporary Seychelles’ artists trained in universities the world over since the independence of the country in 1976, particularly, have been free to express themselves in a variety of styles. </p>
      <p>Painters have traditionally taken inspiration from the richness of Seychelles’ natural beauty to produce a wide range of works using mediums ranging from water-colours to oils, acrylics, collages, metals, aluminium, wood, fabrics, gouache, varnishes, recycled materials, pastels, charcoal, embossing, etching, and giclee prints. Local sculptors produce fine works in wood, stone, bronze and cartonnage. </p>
      <p>Recently published hardback books provide unique overviews of both contemporary art in Seychelles as well as exploring aspects of the history and development of visual art. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Seychelles" title="Music of Seychelles">Music of Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Music and dance have always played a prominent role in Seychelles culture and in all types of local festivities. Rooted in African, Malagasy and European cultures, music is played to the accompaniment of drums such as the Tambour and Tam-Tam and simple string instruments. The violin and guitar are relatively recent foreign imports which play a prominent role in today's music. </p>
      <p>The lively Sega dance with its elegant hip-swaying and shuffling of the feet is still popular as is the traditional Moutya, a mysterious, dance dating back to the days of slavery when it was often used as an outlet for strong emotions and as a way of expressing discontent. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Seychelles" title="Music of Seychelles">music of Seychelles</a> is diverse, a reflection of the fusion of cultures through its history. The <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> of the islands incorporates multiple influences in a syncretic fashion, including African rhythms, aesthetic and instrumentation—such as the zez and the bom (known in Brazil as <a href="/wiki/Berimbau" title="Berimbau">berimbau</a>), European <a href="/wiki/Contredanse_(organisation)" title="Contredanse (organisation)">contredanse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polka" title="Polka">polka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazurka" title="Mazurka">mazurka</a>, French folk and pop, <a href="/wiki/Sega_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Sega music">sega</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> and Réunion, <a href="/wiki/Taarab" title="Taarab">taarab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">soukous</a> and other pan-African genres, and <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_India" title="Music of India">Indian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arcadia_(regional_unit)" title="Arcadia (regional unit)">Arcadian</a> music. </p>
      <p>A form of percussion music called contombley is popular, as is <a href="/wiki/Moutya" class="mw-redirect" title="Moutya">Moutya</a>, a fusion of native folk rhythms with Kenyan <a href="/wiki/Benga_music" title="Benga music">benga</a>. Kontredans (based on European contredanse) is popular, especially in District and School competitions during the annual Festival Kreol (International Creole Festival). Moutya playing and dancing can often be seen at beach bazaars. Their main languages are <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole" title="Seychellois Creole">Seychellois Creole</a> of the French language, French and English. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Seychelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Seychelles">Cuisine of Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg/220px-Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg/330px-Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg/440px-Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1615" data-file-height="1703"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cutting open young coconuts for drinking, Seychelles
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Staple foods include fish, seafood and <a href="/wiki/Shellfish" title="Shellfish">shellfish</a> dishes, often accompanied with rice.<sup id="cite_ref-Lonely_Planet_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lonely_Planet-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Evans_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-59">[59]</a></sup> Fish dishes are cooked in several ways, such as steamed, <a href="/wiki/Grilling" title="Grilling">grilled</a>, wrapped in <a href="/wiki/Banana_leaves" class="mw-redirect" title="Banana leaves">banana leaves</a>, baked, salted and <a href="/wiki/Smoking_(cooking)" title="Smoking (cooking)">smoked</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lonely_Planet_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lonely_Planet-58">[58]</a></sup> Curry dishes with rice are also a significant aspect of the country's cuisine.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PT_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PT-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Additional food staples include coconut, <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mangoes</a> and <i>kordonnyen fish</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tingay_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tingay-61">[61]</a></sup> Dishes are often garnished with fresh flowers.<sup id="cite_ref-Tingay_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tingay-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Chicken dishes, such as chicken curry and <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-59">[59]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Coconut curry<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-59">[59]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Dal" title="Dal">Dhal</a> (lentils)<sup id="cite_ref-Tingay_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tingay-61">[61]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Fish curry<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-59">[59]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saffron_rice" title="Saffron rice">Saffron rice</a><sup id="cite_ref-Tingay_61-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tingay-61">[61]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Fresh <a href="/wiki/Tropical_fruit" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical fruit">tropical fruits</a><sup id="cite_ref-Lonely_Planet_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lonely_Planet-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GOT_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GOT-62">[62]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ladob" title="Ladob">Ladob</a> is eaten either as a savoury dish or as a dessert. The dessert version usually consists of ripe <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweet potatoes">sweet potatoes</a> (but may also include <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a> or even <a href="/wiki/Soursop" title="Soursop">corossol</a>) boiled with coconut milk, sugar, <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> and vanilla in the form of a pod until the fruit is soft and the sauce is creamy.<sup id="cite_ref-Carpin_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carpin-63">[63]</a></sup> The savoury dish usually includes salted fish, cooked in a similar fashion to the dessert version, with plantain, cassava and breadfruit, but with salt used in place of sugar (and omitting vanilla).</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Shark_chutney" title="Shark chutney">Shark chutney</a> typically consists of boiled skinned shark, finely mashed, and cooked with squeezed <a href="/wiki/Bilimbi" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilimbi">bilimbi</a> juice and <a href="/wiki/Lime_(fruit)" title="Lime (fruit)">lime</a>. It is mixed with onion and spices, and the onion is fried and it is cooked in oil.<sup id="cite_ref-Carpin_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carpin-63">[63]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Vegetables<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_59-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GOT_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GOT-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_and_telecommunications_in_Seychelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Media and telecommunications in Seychelles">Media and telecommunications in Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The main daily newspaper is the <i><a href="/wiki/Seychelles_Nation" title="Seychelles Nation">Seychelles Nation</a></i>, dedicated to local government views and current affairs and topics. Other political parties operate other papers such as <i>Regar</i>. Foreign newspapers and magazines are readily available in most bookshops and newsagents. The papers are mostly written in <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole" title="Seychellois Creole">Seychellois Creole</a>, French and English. </p>
      <p>The main television and radio network is operated by the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Seychelles Broadcasting Corporation">Seychelles Broadcasting Corporation</a> which offers locally produced news and discussion programmes in the Seychellois Creole language. Broadcasts run between 3&nbsp;pm and 11:30&nbsp;pm on weekdays and longer hours during the weekends. There are also imported English and French language television programmes on Seychellois terrestrial television and international satellite television has grown rapidly in recent years. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Seychelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Sport in Seychelles">Sport in Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The most popular sport in Seychelles is <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, which has particularly developed last decade.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The country's <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Seychelles national basketball team">national team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2015_African_Games" title="Basketball at the 2015 African Games">2015 African Games</a>, its greatest accomplishment to date. There, the team competed against some of the continent's largest countries such as <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Egypt national basketball team">Egypt</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Women">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Seychelles" title="Women in Seychelles">Women in Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg/170px-Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg/255px-Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg/340px-Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1712" data-file-height="2288"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The district clock tower in the centre of the capital <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Seychellois society is essentially <a href="/wiki/Matriarchy" title="Matriarchy">matriarchal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hr_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hr-66">[66]</a></sup> Mothers tend to be dominant in the household, controlling most expenditures and looking after the interests of the children.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-65">[65]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Unwed_mother" class="mw-redirect" title="Unwed mother">Unwed mothers</a> are the societal norm, and the law requires fathers to <a href="/wiki/Child_support" title="Child support">support their children</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hr_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hr-66">[66]</a></sup> Men are important for their earning ability, but their domestic role is relatively peripheral.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-65">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Seychelles" title="Education in Seychelles">Education in Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Until the mid-19th century, little formal education was available in Seychelles. The Catholic and Anglican churches opened mission schools in 1851. The Catholic mission later operated boys' and girls' secondary schools with religious brothers and nuns from abroad even after the government became responsible for them in 1944. </p>
      <p>A teacher training college opened in 1959, when the supply of locally trained teachers began to grow, and in short time many new schools were established. Since 1981 a system of free education has been in effect, requiring attendance by all children in grades one to nine, beginning at age five. Ninety percent of all children attend nursery school at age four. </p>
      <p>The literacy rate for school-age children rose to more than 90% by the late 1980s. Many older Seychellois had not been taught to read or write in their childhood; adult education classes helped raise adult literacy from 60% to a claimed 100% in 2014. </p>
      <p>There are a total of 68 schools in Seychelles. The public school system consists of 23 <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">crèches</a>, 25 primary schools and 13 secondary schools. They are located on <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_Seychelles" title="Mahé, Seychelles">Mahé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Praslin" title="Praslin">Praslin</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Digue" title="La Digue">La Digue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silhouette_Island" title="Silhouette Island">Silhouette</a>. Additionally, there are three private schools: École Française, International School and the independent school. All the private schools are on Mahé, and the International School has a branch on <a href="/wiki/Praslin" title="Praslin">Praslin</a>. There are seven post-secondary (non-tertiary) schools: the Seychelles Polytechnic, School of Advanced Level Studies, Seychelles Tourism Academy, University of Seychelles Education, Seychelles <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Technology">Institute of Technology</a>, Maritime Training Center, Seychelles Agricultural and Horticultural Training Center and the National Institute for Health and Social Studies. </p>
      <p>The administration launched plans to open a university in an attempt to slow down the <a href="/wiki/Brain_drain" class="mw-redirect" title="Brain drain">brain drain</a> that has occurred. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Seychelles" title="University of Seychelles">University of Seychelles</a>, initiated in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a>, opened on 17 September 2009 in three locations, and offers qualifications from the University of London. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Seychelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Seychelles">Military of Seychelles</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria,_Seychelles.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG/220px-INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG/330px-INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG/440px-INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="625"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria,_Seychelles.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/INS_Teg" title="INS Teg">INS&nbsp;<i>Teg</i></a> approaching Port Victoria, Seychelles
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Military of Seychelles is the Seychelles People's Defence Force which consists of a number of distinct branches: an Infantry Unit and Coast Guard, Air Force and a Presidential Protection Unit. India has played and continues to play a key role developing the military of Seychelles. After handing over two <a href="/wiki/Trinkat-class_patrol_vessel" title="Trinkat-class patrol vessel">SDB Mk5 patrol vessels</a> built by <a href="/wiki/GRSE" class="mw-redirect" title="GRSE">GRSE</a>, the INS Tarasa and INS Tarmugli, to the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_Coast_Guard" title="Seychelles Coast Guard">Seychelles Coast Guard</a>, which were subsequently renamed SCG Constant and SCG Topaz, India also gifted a <a href="/wiki/Dornier_Flugzeugwerke" title="Dornier Flugzeugwerke">Dornier</a> Maritime Patrol aircraft built by <a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Aeronautics_Limited" title="Hindustan Aeronautics Limited">Hindustan Aeronautics Limited</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> India also signed a pact to develop <a href="/wiki/Assumption_Island" title="Assumption Island">Assumption Island</a>, one of the 115 islands that make up the country. Spread over 11&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (4&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), it is strategically located in the Indian Ocean, north of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>. The island is being leased for the development of strategic assets by India.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In 2018, Seychelles signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incarceration">Incarceration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Incarceration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_incarceration_rate" title="List of countries by incarceration rate">List of countries by incarceration rate</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2014, Seychelles had the highest incarceration rate in the world of 799 prisoners per 100,000 population, exceeding the United States' rate by 15%.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> However, the country's actual population is less than 100,000; as of September 2014, Seychelles had 735 actual prisoners, 6% of whom were female, incarcerated in three prisons.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_piracy">Modern piracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Modern piracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Seychelles is a key participant in the fight against Indian Ocean <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a> primarily committed by <a href="/wiki/Piracy_off_the_coast_of_Somalia#Effects_and_perceptions" title="Piracy off the coast of Somalia">Somali pirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wc_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wc-73">[73]</a></sup> Former president <a href="/wiki/James_Michel" title="James Michel">James Michel</a> said that piracy costs between $7&nbsp;million – $12&nbsp;million a year to the international community: "The pirates cost 4% of the Seychelles <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>, including direct and indirect costs for the loss of boats, fishing, and tourism, and the indirect investment for the maritime security." These are factors affecting local fishing – one of the country's main national resources – which had a 46% loss in 2008–2009.<sup id="cite_ref-wc_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wc-73">[73]</a></sup> International contributions of patrol boats, planes or drones have been provided to help Seychelles combat sea piracy.<sup id="cite_ref-wc_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wc-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
